# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes CNI Network Plugin Interface Architecture

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the CNI (Container Network Interface) integration: the CNI plugin invocation, the network namespace setup, the IP address management (IPAM) call, and the network plugin manager that coordinates CNI calls during pod creation.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Kubernetes CNI Network Plugin Interface Architecture and created a comprehensive answer document at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

The analysis reveals that Kubernetes orchestrates CNI integration through a clean separation of concerns:

### Key Components Found:

1. **Pod Sandbox Creation** - `kuberuntime_sandbox.go::createPodSandbox()`
   - Entry point for pod network setup
   - Delegates CNI invocation to the container runtime

2. **Network Configuration** - `kuberuntime_sandbox.go::generatePodSandboxConfig()`
   - Sets up network namespace configuration
   - Passed to container runtime (containerd/cri-o)

3. **IP Retrieval** - `kuberuntime_sandbox.go::determinePodSandboxIPs()`
   - Gets allocated IPs from runtime after sandbox creation
   - Retrieves IPAM-assigned addresses

4. **Node-Level IPAM** - `pkg/controller/nodeipam/`
   - Allocates pod CIDR ranges to nodes
   - `RangeAllocator::AllocateOrOccupyCIDR()` manages subnet distribution

5. **CRI Protocol** - `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.proto`
   - `PodSandboxNetworkStatus` message carries network information
   - Defines the interface between kubelet and container runtime

6. **Pod IP Normalization** - `kubelet_pods.go::sortPodIPs()`
   - Normalizes and sorts pod IPs by family preference
   - Updates pod status for cluster routing

The document includes the complete call chain, file paths, symbol names, and a detailed narrative explanation of how these components work together to implement CNI integration in Kubernetes.

Pod IP Sorting and Normalization\\n**File**: pkg/kubelet/kubelet_pods.go\\n**Function**: `sortPodIPs()` (line 2039)\\n\\nNormalizes pod IPs:\\n- Sorts IPs by IP family preference (IPv4 vs IPv6)\\n- Returns up to 2 IPs (one per IP family)\\n- Updates pod status with properly formatted IPs for cluster routing\\n\\n### 6. Node-Level IPAM (Pod CIDR Allocation)\\n**File**: pkg/controller/nodeipam/node_ipam_controller.go\\n**Type**: `Controller` (line 44)\\n\\nManages cluster-wide IP allocation:\\n- Allocates pod CIDR ranges to nodes\\n- Syncs with cloud provider (if configured)\\n- Uses `legacyIPAM` or `cidrAllocator` based on configuration\\n\\n### 7. CNI plugin calls local IPAM to allocate IP from node's pod CIDR\\n   - Returns IP to runtime\\n4. **Network Status Retrieval** \u2192 determinePodSandboxIPs()\\n   - Extracts IP from PodSandboxNetworkStatus\\n5. **Pod Status Update** \u2192 kubelet updates pod.Status.PodIPs\\n   - Calls sortPodIPs() to normalize IPs\\n   - Reports pod IP to API server\\n\\n## IPAM Flow\\n\\n1. **Node-Level Allocation**: \\n   - NodeIPAM controller allocates /24 (or similar) CIDR to each node\\n   - Allocations tracked locally by IPAM on the node\\n\\n3. **Network Plugin Coordination**:\\n   - CNI plugins use the network namespace created by the runtime\\n   - CNI plugins configure interfaces and routing\\n   - Pod IP Sorting and Normalization\\n**File**: pkg/kubelet/kubelet_pods.go\\n**Function**: `sortPodIPs()` (line 2039)\\n\\nNormalizes pod IPs:\\n- Sorts IPs by IP family preference (IPv4 vs IPv6)\\n- Returns up to 2 IPs (one per IP family)\\n- Updates pod status with properly formatted IPs for cluster routing\\n\\n### 6. Node-Level IPAM (Pod CIDR Allocation)\\n**File**: pkg/controller/nodeipam/node_ipam_controller.go\\n**Type**: `Controller` (line 44)\\n\\nManages cluster-wide IP allocation:\\n- Allocates pod CIDR ranges to nodes\\n- Syncs with cloud provider (if configured)\\n- Uses `legacyIPAM` or `cidrAllocator` based on configuration\\n\\n### 7. Pod CIDR Range Allocation\\n**File**: pkg/controller/nodeipam/ipam/range_allocator.go\\n**Type**: `rangeAllocator` (line 47)\\n**Function**: `AllocateOrOccupyCIDR()` (line 316)\\n\\nAllocates CIDR ranges to nodes:\\n- Assigns subnet ranges from the cluster CIDR to individual nodes\\n- CNI IPAM plugins use this node CIDR to allocate individual pod IPs\\n- Manages both IPv4 and IPv6 CIDR allocation\\n\\n## Call Chain\\n\\n1. **Pod Creation Request** \u2192 kubelet.syncPod()\\n2. **Sandbox Creation** \u2192 kubeGenericRuntimeManager.createPodSandbox()\\n   - Generates PodSandboxConfig with network settings\\n   - Calls runtimeService.RunPodSandbox()\\n3. **Container Runtime (containerd/crio)** executes:\\n   - Creates network namespace\\n   - Invokes CNI plugin executable\\n   - CNI plugin calls local IPAM to allocate IP from node's pod CIDR\\n   - Returns IP to runtime\\n4. **Network Status Retrieval** \u2192 determinePodSandboxIPs()\\n   - Extracts IP from PodSandboxNetworkStatus\\n5. **Pod Status Update** \u2192 kubelet updates pod.Status.PodIPs\\n   - Calls sortPodIPs() to normalize IPs\\n   - Reports pod IP to API server\\n\\n## IPAM Flow\\n\\n1. **Node-Level Allocation**: \\n   - NodeIPAM controller allocates /24 (or similar) CIDR to each node\\n   - Kubelet passes this to container runtime via configuration\\n\\n2. **Pod-Level Allocation**:\\n   - CNI plugins receive the node CIDR\\n   - CNI IPAM (typically \\\"host-local\\\" plugin) allocates individual IPs from this range\\n   - Allocations tracked locally by IPAM on the node\\n\\n3. **Network Plugin Coordination**:\\n   - CNI plugins use the network namespace created by the runtime\\n   - CNI plugins configure interfaces and routing\\n   - Network status returned to kubelet for pod status reporting\\n\\n## Key Files Summary\\n\\n- **Pod creation coordination**: kuberuntime_sandbox.go, kuberuntime_manager.go\\n- **IP retrieval and normalization**: kuberuntime_sandbox.go, kubelet_pods.go\\n- **IPAM at node level**: pkg/controller/nodeipam/ (range_allocator.go, node_ipam_controller.go)\\n- **CRI protocol definitions**: staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.proto\\n- **Runtime interface**: pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go\\n\\nThe architecture cleanly separates concerns: kubelet manages pod lifecycle and IPAM at the cluster level, while container runtimes handle the actual CNI plugin invocation and pod-level IP allocation.\"\n}\n",
